Defending the Absence of Actual Perception in the Additional Attributes View
Refutes an objection about the persistence of additional attributes without actual perception.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand how the view that hearing and sight are additional attributes allows for their persistence even when not actually perceiving, without implying ignorance.

Core Idea
Additional attributes need not be actual to avoid ignorance; they are beyond knowledge.

This passage addresses a specific objection: if hearing and sight are additional attributes, can they exist without actual perception? The objection claims this is like the view of Abu al-Husayn, which was refuted. The commentary defends the additional-attribute view by distinguishing the perception from knowledge, showing that the absence of actual perception does not entail ignorance.

Guided Path
1
Understand the objection
The objector says that allowing the attribute to exist without actual perception is the same as Abu al-Husayn's doctrine, which has been refuted.
Abu al-Husayn's view denied the attributes entirely.
2
Read the answer
The author replies that according to the additional-attribute view, the perception is something beyond knowledge, so its absence does not cause ignorance.
The key is that the attribute is not identical to knowledge.
3
Reflect on the implication
Compare with the case of knowledge: if knowledge were absent, ignorance would follow. But here, the attributes are separate, so no ignorance.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
قوله : ( فإن وصفه تعالى إلخ) وأيضاً قوله : فقالت الفلاسفة إلخ تفصيل لاختلاف المسلمين كما يدل عليه صريح كلام المحصل ثم الظاهر أن المراد بفلاسفة الإسلام، الفلاسفة المتمسكون بأقوال الأنبياء مطلقاً لأن الأنبياء المتقدمين أيضاً قالوا بثبوت السمع والبصر. قوله : ( وإنما لم يوصف بالشم إلخ) قيل : لا خلاف في عدم جواز وصفه تعالى بهذه الثلاثة لعدم ورود النقل لكن إذا ثبت التغاير بين الانكشافين في المسموع والمبصر ثبت التغاير بينهما في المشموم وأمثاله، وإذا ثبت الانكشاف الثاني في المسموع والمبصر له تعالى وجب إثباته في المشموم وأمثاله أيضاً. لئلا يلزم التجهيل تعالى عن ذلك علواً كبيراً. ولذا قال إمام الحرمين: يجب وصفه تعالى بإدراك الطعوم والروائح والحرارة والبرودة كما يجب وصفه تعالى بإدراك المسموع والمبصر للشركة في الدليل لكن لا يقال : إنه تعالى شام ذائق لامس لأنها تنبئ عن الاتصالات الجسمانية. وأنت خبير بأن هذا إنما يتأتى على القول بأن السمع مثلاً نفس العلم بالمسموع، وأما على القول بأنه صفة زائدة ،فلا لأن قياس إثبات الانكشاف الثاني في المشموم وأمثاله له تعالى على إثباته له في المسموع والمبصر مشكل إذ ليس العلة في هذا الإثبات، حينئذ لزوم التجهيز بنفيه. كيف وهذا الانكشاف عند القائل بأن كلاً من السمع والبصر صفة زائدة على الصفات الخمس الباقية ليس علماً حتى يلزم التجهيل من نفيه على أن قابلية الذات للاتصاف بهذه الانكشافات شرط في لزوم التجهيل على تقدير انتفائه ودون إثباتها خرط القتادة . فالعلة فيه ورود النقل المفقود في المشموم وأمثاله . قوله : خروج عن المعقول قالوا ولا ينتقض ذلك بالعالمية والقادرية الأزليتين لأن يصح تعلقها بالمعدوم وبما سيوجد والقادرية يصح تعلقها بأحداث الفعل في الوقت الثاني بخلاف السامعية والمبصرية. العالمية
قوله : ( فإن خلوهما عن الإدراك بالفعل قيل: تجويز خلو الباري عن الإدراك السمعي والبصري مع بقاء منشئهما أعني السمع والبصر مذهب أبي الحسين بعينه وقد أبطلوه. فكيف يلتزمون هذا وجوابه ما أشرنا إليه آنفا من أن الإدراك السمعي والبصري عند من يثبت السمع والبصر صفتين زائدتين أمر وراء العلم فلا يلزم من انتفائهما بالفعل التجهيل كما لزم أبا الحسين على زعمهم فليتأمل
His saying: 'For His description, exalted, etc.' And also his saying: 'For the philosophers said, etc.' is a detailed account of the disagreement among Muslims, as indicated by the explicit words of al-Muhassal. Then it appears that by 'the philosophers of Islam' is meant the philosophers who adhere to the sayings of the prophets absolutely, because the earlier prophets also affirmed hearing and sight. His saying: 'And He is not described with smell, etc.' It is said: There is no disagreement about the impermissibility of describing Him, exalted, with these three due to lack of revelation, but if the distinction between the two disclosures in the heard and seen is established, then the distinction between them in the smelled and its likes is established. And if the second disclosure in the heard and seen is established for Him, exalted, then it is necessary to affirm it in the smelled and its likes as well, lest ignorance be attributed to Him — exalted is He above that greatly. For this reason, Imam al-Haramayn said: It is obligatory to describe Him, exalted, with perception of tastes, smells, heat, and cold, just as it is obligatory to describe Him with perception of the heard and seen due to the commonality in the proof, but it is not said that He is a smeller, taster, toucher, because these indicate physical attachments. And you are aware that this is only feasible on the view that hearing, for example, is the same as knowledge of the heard. But on the view that it is an additional attribute, it is not, because analogizing the affirmation of the second disclosure in the smelled and its likes for Him to its affirmation for Him in the heard and seen is problematic, since the cause for this affirmation is not then the necessity of ignorance by its negation. How so? And this disclosure, according to the one who holds that each of hearing and sight is an additional attribute beyond the remaining five attributes, is not knowledge such that ignorance would follow from its negation, given that the capacity of the essence to be qualified with these disclosures is a condition for the necessity of ignorance assuming its absence, and establishing that is as difficult as cutting a thorn tree. So the cause for it is the revelation that is lacking for smell and its likes. His saying: 'contrary to reason.' They said: And this is not refuted by the eternal will and power, because their relation to non-existent and future existents is valid, and power's relation to the events of the act in the second time is valid, unlike hearing and seeing. 'al-alamiyya'
His saying: 'For their being devoid of actual perception.' It is said: Permitting the absence of auditory and visual perception in the Creator while their sources, i.e., hearing and sight, remain is precisely the doctrine of Abu al-Husayn, and they have refuted it. So how can they adopt this? And its answer is what we pointed to earlier: that auditory and visual perception, according to those who affirm hearing and sight as two additional attributes, is something beyond knowledge, so their absence in actuality does not necessitate ignorance, as it did for Abu al-Husayn, in their view. So reflect.
Source pages p. 102

Commentary
This passage is a lengthy commentary on the sixth section, addressing several points: the classification of philosophers, the disagreement about whether Allah should be described with additional perceptions like smell, taste, and touch based on analogy, the view of Imam al-Haramayn, and the distinction between the views that hearing is identical to knowledge versus an additional attribute. It also responds to an objection about the absence of actual perception, defending that the persistence of the attribute without actual perception does not entail ignorance.

Key Terms
أبي الحسين
صفتين زائدتين

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: One might think that if hearing and sight are attributes, they must always be perceiving something. The text shows they can persist without actual perception.
Correction: The attributes are separate from knowledge; their presence does not require constant perception.

Checkpoint
Why does the absence of actual perception not imply ignorance in the additional-attribute view?
A) Because the attributes are knowledge itself
B) Because perception is something beyond knowledge
C) Because the attributes are eternal
D) Because the objectors are wrong

Key Takeaway
In the additional-attribute view, hearing and sight can exist without actual perception because they are not identical to knowledge.

Proof from Prophetic Consensus that Allah is a Speaker
Sanusi presents the proof from prophetic consensus for Allah's attribute of speech.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand how the consensus of the prophets, transmitted via tawatur, establishes that Allah possesses the attribute of speech.

Core Idea
The prophets' unanimous testimony proves that Allah speaks.

This lesson examines a key proof for the divine attribute of speech (kalam). The author appeals to the consensus (ijma) of all prophets, which is reliably transmitted (mutawatir), to show that they affirmed that Allah commands, forbids, and informs. This consensus provides a compelling transmitted evidence for the attribute.

Guided Path
1
Read the passage
Read the Arabic passage and its translation, noting the structure: observatory, objective, and the proof statement.
The passage is concise; each part is important.
2
Understand the proof
Recognize that the proof is not rational but based on prophetic consensus. This is a transmitted (naqli) evidence.
Contrast with rational proofs for other attributes.
3
Analyze the divisions of speech
The prophets affirmed that Allah commands, forbids, and informs. These are the three divisions of speech, showing that speech is attributed to Allah.
These categories correspond to the types of divine revelation.
4
Reflect on tawatur
The consensus is mutawatir, meaning it is transmitted by so many narrators at each level that falsehood is impossible. This ensures the proof's certainty.
Tawatur is a standard criterion for authenticity in Islamic epistemology.
5
Conclude the claim
From the above, the author concludes that the claim (that Allah is a Speaker) is established. Understand the logical flow: consensus → tawatur → attribution of speech → proof.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
المرصد الرابع - المقصد السابع : في أنه تعالى متكلم . والدليل عليه إجماع الأنبياء عليهم السلام ) فإنه (تواتر أنهم كانوا يثبتون له الكلام، ويقولون : إنه تعالى أمر بكذا ونهى عن كذا وأخبر بكذا وكل من أقسام الكلام فثبت المدعى
The Fourth Observatory - The Seventh Objective: That He, exalted, is a Speaker. The proof for it is the consensus of the prophets, peace be upon them, for it is mutawatir that they affirmed speech for Him and said: He, exalted, commanded such and such, forbade such and such, and informed of such and such, and all of these are divisions of speech. Thus the claim is established.
Source pages p. 103

Commentary
This passage presents the proof that Allah is a Speaker (متكلم). The proof is the consensus (إجماع) of the prophets, which is transmitted via tawatur, indicating that they affirmed speech for Allah in the form of command, prohibition, and information, which are parts of speech. Therefore, the claim is proven.

Key Terms

إجماع الأنبياء
تواتر
أمر
نهى
خبر

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: Some think that Allah's attribute of speech is proven solely by rational argument.
Correction: This passage shows that the proof comes from prophetic consensus, not reason, though rational arguments exist elsewhere.

Checkpoint
What is the proof that Allah is a Speaker according to this passage?
A) Rational argument
B) Consensus of prophets
C) Direct revelation
D) Miracles

Key Takeaway
The prophetic consensus, reliably transmitted, establishes that Allah is a Speaker.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
The prophets unanimously testified that Allah speaks commands, prohibitions, and information. If you truly believe them, why do you still treat His commands as suggestions in your daily life? What specific command have you been ignoring?
?
When you recite the Quran, do you hear it as the direct speech of the One who commands and forbids you, or do you read it passively? Will you commit today to pausing at every verse of command and asking yourself: 'Is this what I am living?'
?
The proof from prophetic consensus leaves no room for doubt that Allah speaks. Yet how often do you act as if His speech is distant or irrelevant? What step will you take tomorrow to bring His words from theory into practice?

The Circularity Objection on Divine Speech
Addresses the circularity objection and distinguishes between speech and miracle.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand the circularity objection against proving divine speech through prophethood and how the answer resolves it by distinguishing between speech and miracle.

Core Idea
The miracle itself verifies the messenger, not Allah's speech.

This passage presents a classic objection in kalam: proving Allah's speech requires the messenger's truthfulness, but proving the messenger's truthfulness requires Allah's speech, creating a circle. The response clarifies that the miracle, not divine speech, confirms the messenger. We'll see how this distinction breaks the circularity.

Guided Path
1
Read the objection carefully
Read the Arabic passage once without analyzing. Then read the translation. Note the structure: objection begins with 'فإن قيل', answer with 'قلنا'.
The objection claims a circular dependency.
2
Understand the alleged circularity
The objection says: messenger's truth depends on Allah's affirmation, and that affirmation is speech. So proving speech through the messenger would be circular.
3
Analyze the answer: miracle as guarantor
The answer denies that affirmation is speech; instead it is the manifestation of a miracle. The miracle itself, not speech, demonstrates the messenger's truthfulness.
The miracle is an independent indicator.
4
Note the two opposed syllogisms
The passage ends by introducing two opposed syllogisms, but the text cuts off. Reflect on how the answer avoids circularity without completing the syllogisms.
The syllogisms would further contrast speech as attribute vs miracle as sign.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
فإن قيل : صدق الرسول موقوف على تصديق الله إياه ) إذ لا طريق إلى معرفته سواه ) وإنه ) أي تصديق الله إياه ( إخباره عن كونه صادقا وهو) أي هذا الإخبار كلام خاص له تعالى ( فإذا قد توقف صدق الرسول على كلامه تعالى ( فإثبات الكلام ) لله سبحانه ( به ) أي بصدق الرسول ( دور قلنا : لا نسلم أن تصديقه له كلام بل هو إظهار المعجزة على وفق دعواه فإنه يدل على صدقه ثبت الكلام ) بأن تكون المعجزة من جنسه كالقرآن الذي يعلم أولاً أنه معجزة خارجة عن قوة البشر ثم يعلم به صدق الدعوى ( أم لم يثبت ) كما إذا كانت المعجزة شيئاً آخر ثم إن هاهنا قياسين متعارضين أحدهما أن كلام الله تعالى صفة له، وكل ما هو
If it is said: The veracity of the messenger depends on Allah's affirming him, for there is no way to know it besides that. And that affirming is His informing that he is truthful, and that informing is a specific speech of His, exalted. So if the veracity of the messenger depends on His speech, then proving speech for Allah by means of the messenger's veracity is circular. We say: We do not concede that affirming him is speech; rather, it is the manifestation of a miracle in accordance with his claim, for it indicates his veracity. Whether the speech is established, as when the miracle is of the same kind as speech, like the Quran, which is first known to be a miracle beyond human power, and then the truth of the claim is known through it, or not established, as when the miracle is something else. Then there are two opposed syllogisms: one is that Allah's speech is an attribute of His, and everything that is...
Source pages p. 103

Commentary
This passage presents an objection that proving Allah's speech through the messenger's veracity leads to circularity. The answer distinguishes between Allah's speech and the miracle that confirms the messenger. The miracle itself demonstrates the messenger's truthfulness without requiring prior knowledge of Allah's speech. The objection and answer are followed by a mention of two opposed syllogisms.

Key Terms

تصديق الرسول
المعجزة

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: Proving Allah's speech through the messenger's veracity leads to an unavoidable circularity.
Correction: The answer shows that the miracle, not divine speech, verifies the messenger, thus no circularity.

Checkpoint

A) By saying the messenger's veracity is self-evident
B) By claiming that Allah's speech is not needed
C) By distinguishing between speech and miracle
D) By denying that the messenger needs affirmation

Key Takeaway
The miracle demonstrates the messenger's truthfulness without requiring prior knowledge of divine speech.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
When you recite the Quran, do you truly see it as a living miracle that demands a response from you right now, or have you grown so familiar with it that its miraculous nature no longer pierces your heart? What would change in your daily life if you treated each verse as a direct sign from Allah calling you to action?
?
The objection in this passage tries to trap believers in a logical circle. Is there any area of your faith where you rely on comfortable assumptions rather than confronting the clear evidence? What would it take for you to break that circle and submit fully to Allah's signs, even when they challenge your habits?
?
Imagine you were standing before the Prophet Muhammad (peace be upon him) and saw a miracle that confirmed his truth. Would you then live differently? The Quran is that same miracle for you today. How are you responding to it? Will you commit this week to read it as fresh revelation and obey its command, or will you let it become just another book?

Affirmation of Divine Speech and Avoiding Circularity
Commentary on speech proof and circularity refutation.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand how the Ash'ari affirmation of divine speech does not lead to circular reasoning in establishing prophethood.

Core Idea
Prophethood can be established without prior divine speech.

In this passage, the commentator addresses a critical objection: if Allah's speech is needed to establish the Law, then proving the Law would require speech, creating a circular argument. He explains that Allah can send messengers through other means, such as creating necessary knowledge in them, without needing to be qualified with speech.

Guided Path
1
Read the passage
Read the Arabic passage carefully. Notice how the commentator first clarifies the Ash'ari position on divine speech and then addresses the circularity objection.
The key claim is that Allah is qualified with speech, not that He creates speech.
2
Identify the objection
The commentator refers to a view from al-Talwih that the establishment of the Law depends on Allah's knowledge, power, and speech. Identify why this could lead to circularity.
3
Understand the refutation
The commentator argues that circularity is avoided because Allah can send messengers through alternative means, like creating necessary knowledge in them or creating sounds, without requiring His own speech.
This shows that prophethood does not depend on divine speech.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
قوله : ( فإنه نواتر أنهم كانوا يثبتون له الكلام أي يثبتون أنه تعالى متصف بالكلام لا أنه موجد له كما تزعمه المعتزلة، ثم أنه لا يتوقف ثبوت الشرع الذي توقف عليه الكلام على الكلام حتى يلزم الدور، إذ يجوز إرسال الرسل بأن يخلق الله تعالى فيهم علماً ضرورياً برسالتهم وما يتعلق بها من الأحكام أو يخلق الأصوات الدالة عليها أو بغير ذلك، ويصدقهم بأن يخلق المعجزة على أيديهم من غير احتياج في شيء من ذلك إلى اتصافه تعالى بالكلام فما ذكر في التلويح من أن ثبوت الشرع موقوف على علمه وقدرته وكلامه تعالى لا توجيه له . قوله : ( إنه معجزة خارجة عن قوة البشر إشارة إلى أن دلالته على الصدق ليست باعتبار أنه كلام حتى يلزم الدور، لا يقال : القرآن الحادث معجزة يدل على القرآن القديم، وهو الكلام النفسي فليس فيه شبهة الدور لأنا نقول : صدق الحادث، إنما يعلم بدلالة المعجزة التي هي نفسها فجاء الدور والمخلص ما ذكر. قوله : (كما إذا كانت المعجزة شيئاً آخر إن قلت : فحينئذ يتوقف أعلى المعجزات وأظهرها على ما هو أدنى منه ولا يخفى بطلانه قلت : الإعجاز في الكلام اللفظي لا الكلام
His saying: 'For it is mutawatir that they affirmed speech for Him' means they affirmed that He, exalted, is qualified with speech, not that He is its originator as the Mu'tazila claim. Then the establishment of the Law, upon which speech depends, does not depend on speech such that circularity would occur, because it is permissible to send messengers by Allah creating in them necessary knowledge of their mission and the rulings related to it, or by creating sounds indicating it, or otherwise, and He confirms them by creating a miracle at their hands without needing in any of that His being qualified with speech. So what is mentioned in al-Talwih, that the establishment of the Law depends on His knowledge, power, and speech, has no basis. His saying: 'It is a miracle beyond human power' indicates that its indication of truthfulness is not because it is speech, such that circularity would occur. It cannot be said: The created Quran is a miracle indicating the eternal Quran, which is the inner speech, so there is no suspicion of circularity, because we say: The truthfulness of the created is only known by the indication of the miracle itself, so circularity occurs, and the solution is what was mentioned. His saying: 'As when the miracle is something else' – if you say: Then the highest and most evident miracle depends on what is lower than it, and its falsity is clear. I say: The miraculousness is in the verbal speech, not the speech...
Source pages p. 103

Commentary
This commentary elaborates on the proof from consensus, clarifying that the prophets affirmed that Allah is qualified with speech, not that He creates speech as the Mu'tazila claim. It also addresses the issue of circularity by noting alternative ways of establishing prophethood without requiring prior speech. It then discusses the miracle of the Quran and the distinction between the created and eternal Quran, emphasizing that the miraculous nature is in the verbal speech.

Key Terms
الكلام
المعتزلة
الدور

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: Some might think that proving prophethood requires Allah's prior speech, leading to circularity.
Correction: The commentator shows that Allah can send messengers through other means, such as creating necessary knowledge in them, avoiding the need for divine speech.

Checkpoint
According to the commentary, how does Allah avoid circularity in establishing the Law?
A) By using His own speech to send messengers
B) By creating necessary knowledge in the messengers
C) By relying on the miracle of the Quran
D) By delegating to the Mu'tazila

Key Takeaway
The Ash'ari position on divine speech does not entail circularity, as prophethood can be established through other means.

The Miracle of the Quran and Its Relation to Eternal Speech
Commentary on Quran's miracle and distinction between created and eternal speech.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand why the Quran's miraculousness is not due to its being speech, and how the distinction between created and eternal speech resolves circularity concerns.

Core Idea
The Quran's miracle is independent of its being divine speech.

This passage continues the discussion on circularity by addressing the Quran itself as a miracle. The commentator argues that the Quran's miraculous nature is separate from its quality as speech; otherwise, circularity would arise. He also addresses an objection about the highest miracle depending on a lower one, and clarifies that the miraculousness lies in the verbal speech, not the eternal inner speech.

Guided Path
1
Read the passage
Read the Arabic passage. Notice how the commentator first asserts that the Quran is a miracle beyond human power, not because it is speech.
2
Follow the objection and response
The commentator presents an objection: if the created Quran is a miracle pointing to the eternal Quran (inner speech), where is the circularity? He then responds that the truthfulness of the created Quran is known by the miracle itself, so circularity remains until resolved by his earlier point.
3
Understand the final point
The commentator addresses a new concern: if the miracle is something else, then the highest miracle (the Quran) depends on something lower. He replies that the miraculousness is in the verbal speech, not the inner speech.
The text ends incomplete, but the main idea is clear.

قوله : ( فإنه نواتر أنهم كانوا يثبتون له الكلام أي يثبتون أنه تعالى متصف بالكلام لا أنه موجد له كما تزعمه المعتزلة، ثم أنه لا يتوقف ثبوت الشرع الذي توقف عليه الكلام على الكلام حتى يلزم الدور، إذ يجوز إرسال الرسل بأن يخلق الله تعالى فيهم علماً ضرورياً برسالتهم وما يتعلق بها من الأحكام أو يخلق الأصوات الدالة عليها أو بغير ذلك، ويصدقهم بأن يخلق المعجزة على أيديهم من غير احتياج في شيء من ذلك إلى اتصافه تعالى بالكلام فما ذكر في التلويح من أن ثبوت الشرع موقوف على علمه وقدرته وكلامه تعالى لا توجيه له . قوله : ( إنه معجزة خارجة عن قوة البشر إشارة إلى أن دلالته على الصدق ليست باعتبار أنه كلام حتى يلزم الدور، لا يقال : القرآن الحادث معجزة يدل على القرآن القديم، وهو الكلام النفسي فليس فيه شبهة الدور لأنا نقول : صدق الحادث، إنما يعلم بدلالة المعجزة التي هي نفسها فجاء الدور والمخلص ما ذكر. قوله : (كما إذا كانت المعجزة شيئاً آخر إن قلت : فحينئذ يتوقف أعلى المعجزات وأظهرها على ما هو أدنى منه ولا يخفى بطلانه قلت : الإعجاز في الكلام اللفظي لا الكلام
His saying: 'For it is mutawatir that they affirmed speech for Him' means they affirmed that He, exalted, is qualified with speech, not that He is its originator as the Mu'tazila claim. Then the establishment of the Law, upon which speech depends, does not depend on speech such that circularity would occur, because it is permissible to send messengers by Allah creating in them necessary knowledge of their mission and the rulings related to it, or by creating sounds indicating it, or otherwise, and He confirms them by creating a miracle at their hands without needing in any of that His being qualified with speech. So what is mentioned in al-Talwih, that the establishment of the Law depends on His knowledge, power, and speech, has no basis. His saying: 'It is a miracle beyond human power' indicates that its indication of truthfulness is not because it is speech, such that circularity would occur. It cannot be said: The created Quran is a miracle indicating the eternal Quran, which is the inner speech, so there is no suspicion of circularity, because we say: The truthfulness of the created is only known by the indication of the miracle itself, so circularity occurs, and the solution is what was mentioned. His saying: 'As when the miracle is something else' – if you say: Then the highest and most evident miracle depends on what is lower than it, and its falsity is clear. I say: The miraculousness is in the verbal speech, not the speech...
Source pages p. 103

Commentary
This commentary elaborates on the proof from consensus, clarifying that the prophets affirmed that Allah is qualified with speech, not that He creates speech as the Mu'tazila claim. It also addresses the issue of circularity by noting alternative ways of establishing prophethood without requiring prior speech. It then discusses the miracle of the Quran and the distinction between the created and eternal Quran, emphasizing that the miraculous nature is in the verbal speech.

القرآن الحادث

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: Some think the Quran's miraculousness is due to its being divine speech, leading to circularity.
Correction: The commentator explains that the miracle is separate; it is the verbal speech that is miraculous, not the eternal inner speech.

Checkpoint
According to the commentary, how does the created Quran's truthfulness become known?
A) By its indication of the eternal Quran
B) By the miracle itself
C) By the consensus of scholars
D) By rational deduction

Key Takeaway
The Quran's miraculousness is in its verbal form, not in its being eternal speech, thus avoiding circularity.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
When you recite the Quran, do you ever pause to consider that its power to move you is not because it is 'God's speech' in the abstract, but because its very words are a miracle beyond what any human could produce? Does this realization change how you approach your daily recitation?
?
How often do you rely on the Quran's miraculous nature as a proof for your faith, only to find yourself caught in circular reasoning when you are asked to defend it? This lesson teaches that the miracle is in the verbal form itself. Have you internalized this, or do you still seek external signs while neglecting the inherent miracle in the words you read?
?
The commentator resolves a deep logical problem. But on a personal level, are you content to accept the Quran's miracle as self-evident, or do you feel the need to prove it to yourself constantly? What does your dependence on external proofs say about your trust in Allah's word?

Proof from Consensus of Prophets for God's Speech
Proof from consensus of prophets for God's speech and resolution of circularity.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand how the consensus of the prophets serves as a proof for God's attribute of speech, and how the objection of circularity is answered by appealing to miracles rather than speech as verification.

Core Idea
The prophets' consensus proves God's speech; the miracle, not speech, verifies the prophet.

This passage presents a key argument for God's attribute of speech: the unanimous testimony of the prophets. However, an objection arises that this reasoning is circular. The response redefines God's verification of the prophet as the miracle itself, not divine speech, thereby breaking the circle.

Guided Path
1
Read the proof from consensus
Read the first part of the passage where the author presents the proof: the prophets' consensus that God speaks.
Notice the claim that their testimony is mutawatir.
2
Identify the circularity objection
Find the objection: if the prophet's truthfulness depends on God's speech, then proving speech by that truthfulness is circular.
3
Understand the answer: miracle as verification
Read the answer: God's verification is not speech but the miracle. The miracle can be of the same kind as speech (like the Qur'an) or something else.
This breaks the circularity.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
المقصد السابع : في أنه تعالى متكلم في أنه تعالى متكلم والدليل عليه إجماع الأنبياء عليهم السلام فإنه تواتر أنهم كانوا يثبتون له الكلام، ويقولون : إنه تعالى أمر بكذا ونهى عن كذا وأخبر بكذا وكل من أقسام الكلام فثبت المدعى فإن قيل : صدق الرسول موقوف على تصديق الله إياه إذ لا طريق إلى معرفته سواه وإنه أي تصديق الله إياه إخباره عن كونه صادقا وهو أي هذا الإخبار كلام خاص له تعالى فإذا قد توقف صدق الرسول على كلامه تعالى فإثبات الكلام لله سبحانه به أي بصدق الرسول دور قلنا : لا نسلم أن تصديقه له كلام بل هو إظهار المعجزة على وفق دعواه فإنه يدل على صدقه ثبت الكلام بأن تكون المعجزة من جنسه كالقرآن الذي يعلم أولاً أنه معجزة خارجة عن قوة البشر ثم يعلم به صدق الدعوى أم لم يثبت كما إذا كانت المعجزة شيئاً آخر قوله : (فإنه نواتر أنهم كانوا يثبتون له الكلام أي يثبتون أنه تعالى متصف بالكلام لا أنه موجد له كما تزعمه المعتزلة، ثم أنه لا يتوقف ثبوت الشرع الذي توقف عليه الكلام على الكلام حتى يلزم الدور، إذ يجوز إرسال الرسل بأن يخلق الله تعالى فيهم علماً ضرورياً برسالتهم وما يتعلق بها من الأحكام أو يخلق الأصوات الدالة عليها أو بغير ذلك، ويصدقهم بأن يخلق المعجزة على أيديهم من غير احتياج في شيء من ذلك إلى اتصافه تعالى بالكلام فما ذكر في التلويح من أن ثبوت الشرع موقوف على علمه وقدرته وكلامه تعالى لا توجيه له . قوله : ( إنه معجزة خارجة عن قوة البشر إشارة إلى أن دلالته على الصدق ليست باعتبار أنه كلام حتى يلزم الدور، لا يقال : القرآن الحادث معجزة يدل على القرآن القديم، وهو الكلام النفسي فليس فيه شبهة الدور لأنا نقول : صدق الحادث، إنما يعلم بدلالة المعجزة التي هي نفسها فجاء الدور والمخلص ما ذكر. قوله : (كما إذا كانت المعجزة شيئاً آخر إن قلت : فحينئذ يتوقف أعلى المعجزات وأظهرها على ما هو أدنى منه ولا يخفى بطلانه قلت : الإعجاز في الكلام اللفظي لا الكلام النفسي وهو الثابت بالشرع المتوقف على ما ذكر على أن الثابت بالإعجاز كون الكلام اللفظي من عند الله تعالى، ويكفي فيه حصوله بأقداره وتمكينه مع عدم إقدار غيره، والثابت بالشرع كونه صفة له تعالى قائمة به على ما هو رأى السلف في الكلام اللفظي أو كونه بإيجاده تعالى بلا واسطة ولو في غيره.
The Seventh Objective: Concerning that He, exalted, is a speaker. (He is a speaker, and the proof for it is the consensus of the prophets, peace be upon them, for it is mutawatir that they used to affirm speech for Him, and they would say: He, exalted, commanded such-and-such, forbade such-and-such, and informed of such-and-such, and all of the divisions of speech, so the claim is proven.) If it is said: The truthfulness of the messenger is dependent on God's verification of him, since there is no way to know it other than that, and that (i.e., God's verification of him) is His informing about him being truthful, and that (i.e., this informing) is specific speech of Him, exalted. So if the truthfulness of the messenger is dependent on His speech, then establishing speech for God, exalted, by it (i.e., by the messenger's truthfulness) is a circularity. We say: We do not grant that His verification of him is speech. Rather, it is the manifestation of a miracle in accordance with his claim, for it indicates his truthfulness, regardless of whether speech is established (by the miracle being of its kind, like the Qur'an which is first known as a miracle beyond human power, then through it the truth of the claim is known) or not established (as when the miracle is something else). His saying: (For it is mutawatir that they used to affirm speech for Him) means they affirm that He, exalted, is described by speech, not that He originates it as the Mu'tazila claim. And then the establishment of the Law, upon which speech depends, does not depend on speech such that circularity would occur, for it is permissible to send messengers by God, exalted, creating in them necessary knowledge of their mission and what pertains to it of rulings, or creating sounds indicating them, or otherwise, and to verify them by creating miracles at their hands without any of that requiring that He be described by speech. So what was mentioned in al-Talwih that the establishment of the Law is dependent on His knowledge, power, and speech—it has no justification. His saying: (It is a miracle beyond human power) is an indication that its indication of truthfulness is not because it is speech such that circularity would occur. It cannot be said: The created Qur'an is a miracle indicating the eternal Qur'an, which is internal speech, so there is no suspicion of circularity, because we say: The truthfulness of the created (Qur'an) is only known through the indication of the miracle which is itself, so circularity arises, and the solution is what was mentioned. His saying: (as when the miracle is something else—if you say: then the highest and most manifest miracles depend on what is lower than it, and its invalidity is not hidden. I say: Inimitability is in verbal speech, not internal speech, and it (internal speech) is established by the Law, which depends on what was mentioned, given that what is established by inimitability is that verbal speech is from God, exalted, and it suffices that it occurs by His decree and enabling along with not enabling others; and what is established by the Law is that it is an attribute of Him, exalted, subsisting in Him according to the view of the Salaf concerning verbal speech, or that it is by His origination without intermediary even if in another.)
Source pages p. 103

Commentary
This passage presents the proof from the consensus of the prophets for God's attribute of speech, an objection of circularity, and its resolution. The passage begins by stating the proof: the prophets unanimously affirmed that God speaks, commands, forbids, and informs—all categories of speech. Thus, the claim that God is a speaker is established. Then an objection is raised: if the prophet's truthfulness is known only through God's verification, and that verification is itself God's speech, then proving God's speech through the prophet's truthfulness would be circular. The answer denies that verification is speech; rather, it is the manifestation of a miracle that confirms the prophet's claim. This miracle may be of the same genus as speech (like the Qur'an) or something else. The commentary then expands: the prophets affirm that God is described by speech, not that He creates it as the Mu'tazila hold. The establishment of the revealed Law does not require God's speech (as an attribute) because God could send messengers by creating direct knowledge in them or by created sounds, and verify them by miracles without needing to be described by speech. The commentary on the miracle of the Qur'an explains that the Qur'an's inimitability proves it is from God, but this does not involve circularity because the inimitability does not depend on the Qur'an being God's attribute. The discussion of the miracle being something else raises a further objection that this would make the highest miracle dependent on a lower one, and the answer distinguishes between verbal speech (mu'jiz) and internal speech (thabit bi al-shar').

Key Terms
إجماع الأنبياء
كلام الله
صدق الرسول
المعجزة
دور

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: One might think the proof for God's speech is circular.
Correction: The passage shows that the miracle, not speech, establishes the prophet's truthfulness, thus breaking the circle.

Checkpoint
How does the passage resolve the charge of circularity in proving God's speech through the prophets?
A) By showing that the prophets' consensus is independent of miracles.
B) By denying that God's verification of the prophet is speech; instead, it is a miracle.
C) By claiming that the prophet's truthfulness is self-evident.
D) By arguing that speech is not an attribute of God.

Key Takeaway
The consensus of the prophets establishes that God speaks, and the miracle verifying the prophet is distinct from God's speech, avoiding circularity.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
You have learned that the prophets' consensus is proof that God speaks. But do you truly live as if God's speech—His commands and prohibitions—are authoritative over every aspect of your life? Think of one command from God that you have been avoiding or justifying away. What is one concrete step you will take today to submit to that command, no matter how hard it feels?
?
The objection in the passage assumed that verifying a prophet must be through speech. Are there areas in your life where you are demanding that God speak to you in a specific way (e.g., a sign, a dream, a feeling) before you believe or obey His revealed word? What sign has God already given you—perhaps a miracle in your own life or the clarity of the Qur'an—that you have ignored because it wasn't in the form you expected?
?
The passage broke the circularity by pointing to the miracle as a clear sign. Have you ever received a clear sign from God—an answered prayer, a provision, a guidance—and yet doubted because you wanted a different kind of proof? What would it take for you to fully trust that God has already given you enough evidence to submit to Him without reservation? Write down one verse or prophetic tradition that you will use as a reminder of God's sufficiency.

Resolving Circularity: The Miracle as Verification and the Nature of Divine Speech
Commentary on the proof and resolution of circularity.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand the detailed resolution of the circularity objection, including the role of the miracle, the distinction between internal and verbal speech, and how the Qur'an's inimitability avoids circularity.

Core Idea
The miracle verifies the prophet without assuming God's speech; verbal speech's inimitability proves its divine origin.

This passage expands on the answer to the circularity objection, clarifying that the establishment of the Law does not require God's attribute of speech, and that the miracle of the Qur'an does not lead to circularity because its inimitability is not based on it being God's speech, but on its content.

Guided Path
1
Understand the expanded commentary on the consensus
Read the commentary explaining that the prophets affirm God is described by speech, not that He creates it, contrary to the Mu'tazila.
This corrects a possible misinterpretation.
2
Follow the argument that the Law does not depend on divine speech
Notice the claim that God could send messengers and verify them without being described by speech, e.g., by creating necessary knowledge or sounds.
This avoids circularity entirely.
3
Examine the distinction between miracle and speech
The commentary says the miracle's indication of truthfulness is not because it is speech, so no circularity. Even the Qur'an, as a miracle, indicates truthfulness without assuming it is God's eternal speech.
4
Understand the solution for the Qur'an
The passage distinguishes between verbal speech (mu'jiz) and internal speech (thabit bi al-shar'). The Qur'an's inimitability proves it is from God, not that it is His attribute.
This resolves the apparent circularity.

⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books

According to the passage, what does the inimitability of the Qur'an prove?
A) That the Qur'an is God's eternal speech.
B) That the Qur'an is from God, but not necessarily that it is His attribute.
C) That the Qur'an is a created thing.
D) That the Qur'an is not a miracle.

Key Takeaway
The miracle of the Qur'an is its inimitability, which does not presuppose that it is God's internal speech, thus avoiding circularity.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
The passage shows that God can verify His messengers through miracles without even needing to speak. Do you truly believe that God's signs in your life—whether through the Qur'an or other means—are sufficient to guide you, or do you demand more? What specific sign are you waiting for that you think He has not given?
?
You recite the Qur'an regularly. But do you approach it merely as a text with rules and stories, or as a living miracle that commands your obedience? What is one area of your life where you have not submitted to its inimitability because you doubt it is truly from God?

Two Conflicting Syllogisms and the Four Sects
Presentation of two conflicting syllogisms on God's speech and division into four sects.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand the two conflicting syllogisms regarding God's speech and how they led to the division of Muslims into four sects.

Core Idea
God's speech: eternal attribute or originated composition? Two arguments, four positions.

This passage presents the core theological debate about the nature of God's speech. Two syllogisms, one for eternity and one for origination, set up a conflict that divided Muslim scholars into four distinct groups. Understanding these arguments is key to grasping later theological discussions.

Guided Path
1
Read the passage carefully
Read the Arabic passage once without analyzing. Then read the translation. Notice how the author presents the two conflicting syllogisms and the resulting division.
The passage is dense; take your time with each part.
2
Identify the two syllogisms
Find the two qiyasatayn muta'aridayn. Note their premises (sughra and kubra) and conclusions. The first argues for eternity, the second for temporality.
The syllogisms are directly stated in the opening lines.
3
Understand the four sects
The passage states that Muslims split into four groups based on which syllogism they accept and which premise they impugn. Map out each group's position.
The Hanbalis are given as an example of one group.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
ثم إن هاهنا قياسين متعارضين أحدهما أن كلام الله تعالى صفة له، وكل ما هو صفة له فهو قديم فكلامه تعالى قديم، وثانيهما أن كلامه مؤلف من أجزاء مترتبة متعاقبة في الوجود وكل ما هو كذلك فهو حادث فكلامه تعالى حادث، فافترق المسلمون إلى فرق أربع : ففرقتان منهم ذهبوا إلى صحة القياس الأول، وقدحت واحدة منهما في صغرى القياس الثاني، وقدحت الأخرى في كبراه وفرقتان أخريان ذهبوا إلى صحة الثاني، وقد حوا في إحدى مقدمتي الأول على التفصيل المذكور، وإلى ما ذكرناه أشار المصنف رحمه الله بقوله : (ثم قال الحنابلة كلامه حرف وصوت يقومان : بذاته وإنه قديم وقد بالغوا فيه حتى قال بعضهم جهلاً : الجلد والغلاف قديمان ) فضلاً المصحف، فهؤلاء صححوا القياس الأول ومنعوا كبرى القياس الثاني قوله: (قدحت الأخرى في كبراه إن حمل تعاقب الوجود المذكور في الصغرى على أن وجود الثاني مشروط بوجود الأول وانقضائه، فالقدح في الكبرى والقول بالقدم تناقض لا يجيء عن عاقل فضلا عن مجتهد مثل الإمام أحمد بن حنبل، والظاهر أن مراده التعاقب في الترتيب كالمكتوب في المصحف على ما أشرنا إليه في أوائل الكتاب، فحينئذ يكون مذهبه عين مذهب السلف الذي سيذكره في آخر البحث ويكون اشتراط وجود كل حرف بانقضاء الآخر بالنظر إلينا لعدم مساعدة الآلة كما سیصرح به.
Then there are two conflicting syllogisms: one of them is that the speech of God, exalted, is an attribute of His, and everything that is an attribute of His is eternal, so His speech is eternal; and the second is that His speech is composed of parts arranged in successive existence, and everything like that is originated, so His speech is originated. So the Muslims divided into four sects: two of them affirmed the validity of the first syllogism, one of them impugned the minor premise of the second syllogism, and the other impugned its major premise; and the other two affirmed the validity of the second syllogism, and they impugned one of the two premises of the first in the detailed manner mentioned. And to what we have mentioned, the author, may God have mercy on him, pointed by his saying: (Then the Hanbalis said: His speech is a letter and a sound subsisting in His essence, and it is eternal, and they exaggerated in that until some of them ignorantly said: the leather and the cover are eternal) let alone the mushaf. These (Hanbalis) affirmed the first syllogism and prevented the major premise of the second. His saying: (The other impugned its major premise) — if the succession of existence mentioned in the minor premise is interpreted as the existence of the second being conditional upon the existence and expiration of the first, then the impugnment of the major premise and the assertion of eternity is a contradiction that would not come from a rational person, let alone a mujtahid like Imam Ahmad ibn Hanbal. The apparent meaning is that he meant succession in order, like what is written in the mushaf, as we pointed out at the beginning of the book. In that case, his doctrine would be the same as the doctrine of the Salaf which he will mention at the end of the discussion, and the condition of the existence of each letter upon the expiration of the other is from our perspective due to the lack of assistance from the instrument, as he will clarify.
Source pages p. 103

Commentary
This passage presents the two conflicting syllogisms concerning God's speech and the resulting division of Muslims into four sects. The passage begins by stating two contradictory analogies: the first argues that since God's speech is an attribute, and every attribute of God is eternal, therefore His speech is eternal. The second argues that since God's speech is composed of parts that follow each other in existence, and everything that follows successively is originated, therefore His speech is originated. These two syllogisms led Muslims to split into four groups. Two groups accepted the first syllogism: one of them rejected the minor premise of the second syllogism (i.e., that speech is composed of successive parts), and the other rejected its major premise (i.e., that everything successive is originated). The other two groups accepted the second syllogism: each of them rejected one of the premises of the first syllogism. The passage then gives the Hanbali position as an example of the group that accepted the first syllogism and rejected the major premise of the second: they believe God's speech consists of letters and sounds subsisting in His essence and is eternal, even claiming that the leather and cover (of the mushaf) are eternal. The commentary on the line 'the other impugned its major premise' clarifies a potential contradiction: if the succession means that each later part depends on the previous one's passing away, then claiming eternity (for the speech) is contradictory. The commentator suggests that the Hanbali view might refer to succession in order (like written words), not in temporal succession, making it compatible with the Salaf view where the condition of each letter's existence upon the expiration of the prior is only from our limited perspective, not in God's essence.

كبرى
حنابلة

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: One might think the Hanbali view that God's speech is eternal but composed of successive parts is inherently contradictory.
Correction: The commentator explains that the succession meant is in order (like written words), not temporal dependence, so there is no contradiction. The condition of each letter's existence upon the prior's expiration is only from our perspective.

Checkpoint
How many groups of Muslims resulted from the two conflicting syllogisms according to the passage?
A) Two
B) Three
C) Four
D) Five

Key Takeaway
The debate over God's speech hinges on two conflicting syllogisms, producing four theological positions; the Hanbali view, properly understood, aligns with the Salaf by interpreting 'succession' as order, not temporal dependence.

How does your belief about its nature affect your reverence and urgency in acting upon it? ?
The Hanbali position has been accused of contradiction. Have you ever dismissed a theological view because of an extreme fringe statement? Your attitude in such matters reflects your sincerity in seeking truth.

The Refutation of the Hanbali View on God's Speech
Refutation of the Hanbali claim that God's speech consists of eternal letters and sounds

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand why the Hanbali claim that God's speech consists of eternal letters and sounds is invalid, based on the logical analysis of the letters' dependence on one another.

Core Idea
If a letter depends on the prior letter's end, it has a beginning and cannot be eternal.

In this passage, Sanusi refutes the Hanbali claim that the Qur'an (as God's speech) is composed of eternal letters and sounds. He argues that each letter's existence is conditioned on the expiration of the preceding letter, which gives it a temporal beginning and thus proves it is originated (hadith). This logical argument exposes the inconsistency in the Hanbali view. The passage also addresses more extreme claims that the physical book or its cover are eternal, dismissing them as ignorance.

Guided Path
1
Understand the Hanbali claim
The Hanbalis assert that God's speech consists of eternal letters and sounds. Read the passage to see how this claim is framed.
The passage calls this view 'invalid necessarily'.
2
Analyze the logic for the non-first letters
The argument shows that each letter (beyond the first) is conditioned on the previous letter's expiration, which gives it a beginning. Thus it cannot be eternal.
Pay attention to the phrase 'فإن حصول كل حرف مشروط بانقضاء الآخر'.
3
Consider the case of the first and last letters
The first letter is not conditioned on a prior one, but the last letter has an expiration, proving its origination. Therefore all letters are originated.
The commentary clarifies that the inference relies on the principle that the eternal cannot cease.
4
Reflect on the extreme Hanbali claims
The passage dismisses claims that the leather cover or the written mushaf are eternal, attributing them to ignorance.
Understand why such views are considered inconsistent with the earlier argument.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
وهذا باطل بالضرورة فإن حصول كل حرف من الحروف التي تركب منها كلامه على زعمهم مشرط بانقضاء الآخر منها فيكون (له) أي للحرف المشروط ( أول فلا يكون قديماً)، وكذا يكون للحرف الآخر انقضاء فلا يكون هو أيضاً قديماً بل حادثاً ( فكذا المجموع المركب منها أي من الحروف التي لها أول زمان وجوداً وآخره أو عن قوله: (فإن حصول كل حرف مشروط بانقضاء الآخر الظاهر أن مراده من كل ما سوى الحرف الأول فإنه غير مشروط بانقضاء الآخر إذ ليس قبله حرف، ولذا استدل على حدوث الحرف الآخر بأن له انقضاء لا بأن لها أول كما في الحرف المتوسط مع أن استدلاله ذلك مبني على أن ما ثبت قدمه امتنع عدمه وإلا فلا دلالة للانقضاء على الحدوث. قوله: (حتى قال بعضهم جهلاً الجلد والغلاف قديمان كأنهم يزعمون أن الجلد والغلاف كانا كامنين قديمين فبرزا بعمل المجلد وأما ما نقل عن بعضهم من أن الجسم الذي كتب به القرآن فانتظم حروفاً ورقوماً هو بعينه كلام الله تعالى وقد صار قديماً بعدما كان حادثاً فمعناه قد ظهر قدمه بعدما كان في صورة الحادث وعلى أي معنى حمل كلامهم لا يخرج عن كونه من آثار جهلهم.
And this is invalid necessarily, because the occurrence of each letter of the letters from which His speech is composed, according to their claim, is conditioned upon the expiration of the other from it. So (for it), i.e., for the conditioned letter, there is a beginning, so it cannot be eternal. Likewise, for the other letter there is an expiration, so it also is not eternal, but originated. So too the aggregate composed of them, i.e., of the letters which have a beginning in time of existence and an end. Or about— His saying: (For the occurrence of each letter is conditioned upon the expiration of the other) — the apparent meaning is that he means every letter except the first, for it is not conditioned upon the expiration of another since there is no letter before it. Hence he deduces the origination of the other letter by its having an expiration, not by its having a beginning as in the middle letter. And his inference is based on the principle that what is established as eternal is impossible to cease; otherwise expiration does not indicate origination. His saying: (Until some of them ignorantly said: the leather and the cover are eternal) — it is as if they claim that the leather and the cover were latent eternally and then emerged by the binder's work. As for what is transmitted from some of them, that the body with which the Qur'an was written, which arranged letters and signs, is itself the speech of God, exalted, and became eternal after it had been originated, its meaning is that its eternity appeared after it had been in the form of the originated. On whatever meaning their speech is interpreted, it does not leave being among the effects of their ignorance.
Source pages p. 104

Commentary
This passage refutes the Hanbali view that God's speech consists of eternal letters and sounds. The refutation argues that if each letter (except possibly the first) is conditioned upon the expiration of the preceding letter, then each such letter has a beginning (since it starts after the previous one ends) and thus cannot be eternal. Moreover, the last letter has an expiration, so it is also originated. Therefore, the whole aggregate of letters is originated. The commentary then clarifies that the argument applies to all letters except the first, which is not conditioned on anything prior. It notes that the inference that the other letter is originated because it has an expiration relies on the principle that what is eternal cannot cease to exist; otherwise, expiration alone does not prove origination. The passage also addresses an extreme Hanbali claim that the physical leather and cover of the mushaf are eternal, dismissing it as ignorance. It explains that such claims stem from the idea that the material objects were latent eternally and then became manifest, or that the inscribed body became eternal after being originated—both of which are rejected as products of ignorance.

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: That the letters of God's speech can be eternal even though each letter (except the first) only occurs after the previous one ends.
Correction: The passage shows that such dependence gives the letter a beginning in time, and since the eternal cannot have a beginning, the letter cannot be eternal. Moreover, the last letter's expiration also indicates its origination.

Key Takeaway
The Hanbali claim that God's speech consists of eternal letters fails because the sequential dependence of letters necessitates origination.

Kalam Nafsi as a Distinct Attribute
Proves kalam nafsi is a third attribute distinct from knowledge and will, with objections and answers.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand the evidence that kalam nafsi is a third divine attribute irreducible to knowledge or will, and the responses to key objections.

Core Idea
Kalam nafsi is not knowledge or will—it is a distinct attribute proven by commands without intent.

After learning about the divine attributes of knowledge and will, the question arises whether God's speech is reducible to these. In this passage, the author argues that kalam nafsi (psychic speech) is a distinct attribute, using the example of commanding without willing. He also addresses objections and counterarguments, solidifying the Ash'ari position.

Guided Path
1
Read the Arabic passage and translation
Carefully read the Arabic source and its English translation. Notice how the passage moves from examples to objections to conclusions.
Pay attention to the initial examples of command without will.
2
Identify the main claim and initial evidence
The author argues that psychic meaning (kalam nafsi) is other than will, using cases where a person commands something they do not will. Observe how this leads to the conclusion that kalam nafsi is a third attribute.
The examples of the testing master and the excusing beater illustrate this.
3
Analyze the objections and responses
The passage includes an objection that these cases involve only the form of command, not reality. The author counters by asserting that the psychic meaning expressed in reports and commands is a third attribute. Later, objections concerning knowledge and analogy are addressed.
Consider the distinction between assertoric and conceptual knowledge.
4
Examine the proof from the command to the disbeliever
The passage argues that God's command to the disbeliever to believe, without willing faith, proves the distinctness of command from will. Understand why this is a decisive argument.
If God had willed faith, it would occur; therefore command and will are different.

المرصد الرابع - المقصد السابع : في أنه تعالى متكلم

قوله : ( هو إرادة فعل إلخ) قيل : هذا توجيه ركيك لأن الكلام النفسي ما يعبر عنه بالعبارات والألفاظ إنما يعبر بها عن معانيها الوضعية، ومن البين أن الإرادة المذكورة ليست مدلولاً وضعياً
The Fourth Observatory - the Seventh Objective: Concerning that He, exalted, is a speaker. He intends it: the psychic meaning which is the command is other than will, because a man may command what he does not will, like the one testing his slave whether he obeys him or not, for his purpose is merely the test, not the performance of the commanded act, and like the one excusing himself for beating his slave due to his disobedience, for he may command him while he wills that he not do the commanded act, to show his excuse to the one blaming him. And it was objected that what exists in these two cases is the form of command, not its reality, for there is no request (talab) in them at all, just as there is definitely no will. So then it (i.e., the psychic meaning which is expressed by the forms of report and command) is a third attribute, other than knowledge and will, subsisting in the soul. Then we claim that it is eternal, due to the impossibility of originated things subsisting in His essence, exalted. The author (al-Mawaqif) said: 'And if the Mu'tazila said that it (i.e., the psychic meaning which is other than expressions in report and command) is a will for an act that becomes a cause for the addressee's belief in the speaker's knowledge of what he reported, or becomes a cause for his belief in his will for what passed by him, it would not be far-fetched, because will for an act is likewise...' His remark: ('for indeed a man may report about what he does not know, rather knows its contrary') It was objected that what follows from the speech, assuming completeness, is that psychic speech is other than certain knowledge, not absolute knowledge; for every rational person about to report must necessarily have in his mind a picture of what he reports, but this is not complete concerning Him, exalted, and analogizing the absent to the witnessed does not establish the desired, though it provides a binding argument against the opponent who holds it. The answer to the first [objection] is that what is fit to be the meaning of informative speech must be assertoric knowledge (ilm tasdiqi), not conceptual (tasawwuri); thus in the mentioned example, if the informant knows the contrary of what he reports, he cannot have any assertoric knowledge of what he reports. Moreover, the purpose is to refute the claim of the Mu'tazila who say that psychic speech in the Necessary, exalted, is nothing but His knowledge; so the otherness of psychic speech from certain knowledge is precisely what is desired. Imam al-Razi answered the second [objection]: because report, since it is other than knowledge in the witnessed, is also other in the absent, due to consensus that their essences do not differ in the witnessed and the absent. But you are aware that the absence of difference is not conceded. It may be said in answer: the purpose is merely to depict psychic speech and the modality of its essence; as for its affirmation for the Necessary, it is by what is transmitted from the prophets by tawatur. There is in it that it does not repel the objection, because the depiction mentioned in the witnessed and what is transmitted from the prophets, peace be upon them, provides its affirmation for the Necessary, but does not provide its essence and its otherness from the remaining attributes. His remark: ('and it was objected that what exists etc.') One may be laborious in answering it that this is mentioned as an obliging argument against those who say that the command of a person to another is an expression of the form 'if'al' (do) by way of superiority and dominance, whether or not there is a requiring meaning in the soul. As for the proof of otherness if request is considered in the reality of command, it is that God, exalted, commanded the disbeliever to believe and did not will faith from him. As for the first [the command], because He promised him reward for faith and threatened him with punishment for leaving it; as for the second [that He did not will it], because it is established by proof that will is the attribute that particularizes one of the two possibilities to occur, so if He willed his faith, it would occur. His remark: ('it is a will for an act etc.') It is said: this is a weak interpretation, because psychic speech is what is expressed by expressions and words; they are only used to express their conventional meanings, and it is evident that the mentioned will is not a conventional meaning (madlul wad'i).
Source pages p. 107

Commentary
This passage proves that kalam nafsi (psychic speech) is a third attribute distinct from knowledge (ilm) and will (irada), and responds to objections. It begins by defining the psychic meaning of command (amr) as other than will, giving examples: a man testing his slave commands something he does not will; a man excusing himself for beating his slave commands while willing the opposite. An objection is raised that these cases involve only the form of command, not its reality, since there is no genuine request. The passage then concludes that the psychic meaning expressed in reports and commands is a third attribute (sifa thalitha) other than knowledge and will, subsisting in the soul, and eternal because originated attributes cannot subsist in God. The author then mentions a possible Mu'tazili position that psychic speech might be reduced to will for an act that causes belief, but this is deemed weak. The commentary addresses objections: first, that the argument only shows otherness from certain knowledge, not absolute knowledge; the answer is that informative speech requires assertoric knowledge (tasdiqi), not mere conceptualization, so if the speaker knows the contrary, no assertoric knowledge is present, and otherness from certain knowledge suffices to refute the Mu'tazila. Second, the analogy from the witnessed to the absent is defended by al-Razi on grounds of consensus that essences do not differ, though this is contested. The commentary also notes that the depiction of psychic speech comes from prophetic transmission, but this does not fully establish its essence. Further discussion argues that God's command to the disbeliever to believe, without willing his faith, proves the distinctness of command from will, because will would necessitate occurrence. Finally, the suggestion that psychic speech might be will is rejected because will is not the conventional meaning of expressions. Thus, the lesson establishes kalam nafsi as irreducible to knowledge or will.

Correction: The passage demonstrates through multiple arguments (command without will, command to disbeliever, linguistic analysis) that kalam nafsi is a distinct third attribute that cannot be identified with knowledge or will.

Checkpoint
Why is the command to the disbeliever to believe used as evidence that kalam nafsi is distinct from will?
A) Because the disbeliever does not believe
B) Because God commanded faith but did not will it, proving command and will are different
C) Because the command is verbal, not psychic
D) Because faith is impossible for the disbeliever

Key Takeaway
Kalam nafsi is an eternal divine attribute distinct from knowledge and will, proven by the possibility of commanding without willing and by the fact that God commanded faith from the disbeliever without willing it.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
You claim to believe that God is a speaker with a psychic command. But when His commands confront your desires—like the command to abandon a sin you love—do you treat that command as a real, present demand from a personal Speaker, or just as a static piece of information you might postpone? Today, what is one command of God you have heard but not yet obeyed because you subtly assume He does not really 'will' it for you right now?
?
The proof shows that God can command without willing the act, as with the disbeliever. If you stand before God tomorrow and He reminds you that He commanded you to pray, while knowing you often omitted it, will you argue that He didn't truly 'will' it from you? Or will you acknowledge that His command carried its own claim on your obedience, regardless of your excuses?
?
Consider the Mu'tazili attempt to reduce kalam nafsi to knowledge or will. Are you yourself guilty of a similar reduction—treating God's speech as merely something you 'know' about or 'intend' to follow, rather than as a distinct, living command that demands a response? If God's word were to disappear from your heart right now, would your life show clear evidence of the difference?

God's Command to the Unbeliever: Command Distinct from Will
Commentator addresses the objection that command without will disproves a separate attribute, using God's command to the unbeliever.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand how the example of God's command to the unbeliever demonstrates that command (al-amr) is distinct from will (al-irada), and how this refutes certain objections.

Core Idea
God's command to the unbeliever proves that command is distinct from will.

The commentator tackles an objection that command without will is impossible. He responds by introducing a key distinction: God commanded the unbeliever to believe but did not will it. This argument solidifies the Ash'ari position on divine attributes. We'll examine the reasoning step by step.

Guided Path
1
Read the passage and translation
Read the Arabic passage once without analyzing. Then read the literal translation. Notice the flow from objection to response.
Pay attention to the key terms: الأمر, الإرادة, الكافر.
2
Identify the two parts of the argument
The passage has an objection and a response. The response contains two premises: the promise/threat and the nature of will as specifying attribute.
3
Understand the definitional context
The commentator notes that the argument works against those who define command merely as the imperative form. For those who include demand (طلب), the proof of distinctness is stronger.
This nuance is important for the full argument.
4
Connect the conclusion to divine attributes
Reflect on why this matters: psychological speech (command) is a distinct attribute from will. God can command what He does not will.
This is a key Ash'ari doctrine.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
قوله : ( واعترض عليه بأن الموجود إلخ، قد يتكلف في الجواب عنه بأن هذا ذكر إلزاماً على من قال : إن أمر الإنسان غيره عبارة عن صيغة أفعل على سبيل العلو والاستعلاء سواء قام بالنفس اقتضاء أم لا، وأما الدليل على المغايرة إذا اعتبر في حقيقة الأمر الطلب فهو أن الله تعالى أمر الكافر بالإيمان ولم يرد منه الإيمان، أما الأول فلانه وعده الثواب بالإيمان وأوعده العقاب بتركه وأما الثاني فلما ثبت بالدليل أن الإرادة هي الصفة المخصصة لأحد المقدورين بالوقوع فلو أراد إيمانه لوقع.
His statement: 'And it was objected that what exists etc.' It may be answered with effort that this is mentioned as an irrefutable argument against one who says that a person's command to another is an expression of the imperative form 'if‘al' in the manner of superiority and dominance, whether or not there is an exigency in the soul. As for the proof of distinctness if demand is considered in the essence of command, it is that God, exalted, commanded the unbeliever to believe and did not will belief from him. As for the first, because He promised reward for belief and threatened punishment for leaving it; and as for the second, because it is established by proof that will is the attribute that specifies one of the two possibilities for occurrence, so if He had willed his belief, it would have occurred.
Source pages p. 107

Commentary
This passage addresses an objection about command without will. The commentator suggests a careful response: the examples serve as an irrefutable argument (إلزام) against those who define command merely as the imperative form 'if‘al' with superiority, regardless of any internal mental state. The real proof of distinctness, when demand (طلب) is considered the essence of command, is God's command to the unbeliever to believe, despite the fact that God does not will that belief from him. The first point is that God promised reward for belief and threatened punishment for unbelief, indicating a genuine command. The second point is that will (إرادة) is the attribute that determines which possible action occurs; if God had willed the unbeliever's belief, it would inevitably have occurred. Since the unbeliever does not believe, God's will for his belief is absent, yet the command exists. Thus psychological speech (the command) is distinct from will.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: Some think that command always implies will, so command cannot exist without will.
Correction: God's command to the unbeliever to believe shows that command can exist without will. God commanded belief but did not will it, proving the attributes are distinct.

Checkpoint
What is the proof that God's command to the unbeliever is distinct from His will?
A) The unbeliever does not obey, so God must have commanded without willing.
B) God promised reward for belief and threatened punishment, but the unbeliever does not believe, so God did not will it.
C) Will is not needed for command.
D) The command is merely a form of words.

Key Takeaway
God's command to the unbeliever to believe, despite the unbeliever's disbelief, proves that the attribute of command is distinct from the attribute of will.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
God commands the unbeliever to believe sincerely, even though He does not will his belief. How does this affect your understanding of God's commands to you? Do you sometimes assume that your failures to obey are because God 'didn't will' your obedience, and thus you are excused? Repent of that excuse and commit to responding to His command as a real demand on you.
?
If God willed your belief, it would inevitably occur. Does your doubt or lack of faith ever make you question whether God truly wills your guidance? Rather than speculating, ask yourself: are you actively responding to the command to believe that He has given you, or are you neglecting it because you think your disbelief is predestined?
?
This lesson shows that command and will are distinct. Think of a specific sin you committed today. God commands you not to do it, yet you did it. Are you tempted to think that because God didn't will otherwise, His command was not genuine? Acknowledge the distinction: His command is real and binding, and your disobedience is your own. How will you change your behavior tomorrow to honor His command?

Resolving the Mu'tazilite Objection on Additional Knowledge
Commentator resolves the Mu'tazilite objection by interpreting 'knowledge' as omniscience.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand how the commentator defends Mu'tazilite consistency by interpreting 'knowledge' as omniscience when speaking of God.

Core Idea
For God, 'knowledge' means omniscience, not a separate attribute.

In this short but dense comment, the author addresses a potential contradiction in the Mu'tazilite position. They deny eternal attributes yet use 'knowledge' to explain speech. The commentator shows that this is not contradictory when 'knowledge' is understood as the state of being all-knowing rather than a distinct entity. Let's unpack this subtle point.

Guided Path
1
Read the objection
Read the first part of the passage where the objection is raised: how can Mu'tazilites affirm additional knowledge when they deny it? Identify the tension.
Focus on the phrase 'this is an explicit affirmation of additional knowledge'.
2
Understand the concession
Note that the commentator first concedes the point is about God's specificity, then offers an interpretation.
The concession is in 'after conceding that the speech concerns the specificity of the Necessary'.
3
Grasp the reinterpretation
Focus on the key move: 'perhaps what is meant by knowledge is omniscience (al-ulamiyya).' Understand the shift from a separate attribute to a state of the essence.
4
Apply the same to will and dislike
Recognize that the same reasoning applies to will and dislike, showing a consistent pattern.
5
Reflect on the subtlety
The author ends with 'ponder' – consider why this is a nuanced point that requires careful thought.
Why might this reinterpretation still be contentious?

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
قوله : ( راجع إلى العلم القائم بالمتكلم إلخ) فإن قلت : هذا تصريح بإثبات العلم الزائد، فكيف تقول به المعتزلة النافون له قلت بعد تسليم أن الكلام في خصوصية الواجب تعالى، لعل المراد بالعلم العالمية وكذا الكلام في الإرادة والكراهة فتأمل.
His statement: 'It refers back to knowledge subsisting in the speaker etc.' Then you say: This is an explicit affirmation of additional knowledge (al-ilm al-za'id), so how can the Mu'tazilites, who deny it, say it? I say: After conceding that the speech concerns the specificity of the Necessary, exalted, perhaps what is meant by knowledge is omniscience (al-ulamiyya), and likewise for will and dislike, so ponder.
Source pages p. 108

Commentary
This final passage addresses a tension: the commentator previously stated that the Mu'tazilites themselves, in their view, make the meanings of expressions refer back to knowledge (for reports) and will (for commands) subsisting in the speaker. But if so, they are affirming an additional attribute (knowledge) beyond the essence, which contradicts their own denial of such attributes. The response is that when dealing with God (الواجب تعالى), the word 'knowledge' (العلم) most likely refers to the attribute of omniscience (العالمية), i.e., the state of being all-knowing, rather than a distinct mental entity. Similarly for will and dislike. Thus, the Mu'tazilite position is not necessarily self-contradictory, because they interpret these terms as expressions of the essence, not as separate attributes. The author invites the reader to reflect (فتأمل) on this subtle point.

الواجب تعالى
الإرادة
الكراهة

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: The Mu'tazilites are inconsistent for using 'knowledge' in their explanation while denying eternal attributes.
Correction: This comment shows that they interpret 'knowledge' as omniscience (a state) rather than a separate entity.

Checkpoint

C) He argues they must accept additional knowledge.
D) He ignores the issue.
