The Attribute of Palm and Its Interpretation
Examines a hadith about God's palm and offers metaphorical interpretations.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand how the attribute of 'palm' (الكف) in a hadith about the Night Journey is interpreted metaphorically to avoid anthropomorphism and affirm divine transcendence.

Core Idea
God's 'palm' is a metaphor for His gentle control, not a bodily limb.

This lesson examines a hadith often cited by anthropomorphists to argue that God has a physical hand. The author presents two acceptable metaphorical interpretations that safeguard God's transcendence while honoring the hadith's spiritual meaning.

Guided Path
1
Read the hadith passage and translation
Start by reading the Arabic passage and its literal translation. Notice the mention of the Night Journey and the description of 'coolness' and 'palm'.
The phrase 'كفه المعراج' is ambiguous; context suggests 'his palm' during the ascension.
2
Identify the two interpretations
The author gives two ways to understand 'palm' (كف): either as a figurative attribute unlike any palm, or as a reference to God's administration (التدبير). Find these in the text.
The second interpretation uses an Arabic idiom: 'so-and-so is in the palm of so-and-so' meaning under his control.
3
Reflect on the purpose of the hadith
Consider why the author says the hadith's purpose is to show God's gentleness and spiritual comfort. Connect this to the rejection of anthropomorphism.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
وقد ورد في حديث ليلة كفه المعراج وضع بين كتفي فوجدت بردها في كبدي ولا يجوز إثبات الجارحة كما ذهبت إليه المشبهة فقيل: هو موصوف بكف لا كالكفوف، وقيل: مؤول بالتدبير يقال: فلان في كف فلان أي في تدبيره فالمقصود من الحديث بيان لطفه في تدبيره له وبيان أنه وجد روح اللطف لأن البرد يطلق على كل روح وراحة
And it has come in the hadith of the night of his ascension (al-miʿrāj): 'He placed between my shoulders and I found its coolness in my liver.' And affirming a bodily organ is not permissible, as the anthropomorphists (al-mushabbiha) hold. So it is said: He is described with a palm (kaf) not like palms, and it is said: interpreted by administration (al-tadbīr); it is said: 'So-and-so is in the palm of so-and-so', i.e., in his administration. So the purpose of the hadith is to show His gentleness in His administration for him and to show that he found the spirit of gentleness, because 'cold' (al-bard) is used for every spirit and comfort.
Source pages p. 128

Commentary
This passage addresses the attribute of palm (كف) based on a hadith from the Night Journey where the Prophet felt something cool between his shoulders. The author rejects any literal bodily organ interpretation, aligning with the refutation of anthropomorphism (tashbīh). Two interpretations are given: (1) He is described with a palm that is unlike any palm (i.e., a figurative expression), and (2) it is interpreted as 'administration' (tadbīr), as in the Arabic idiom 'so-and-so is in the palm of so-and-so' meaning under his control. The purpose is to show God's gentle care and the spiritual comfort (rawḥ) the Prophet experienced.

Key Terms
الكف
التأويل
التدبير
البرودة
الروح
المشبهة

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: The hadith proves God has a physical palm.
Correction: The hadith must be interpreted metaphorically to avoid attributing bodily organs to God.

Checkpoint
According to the passage, what is the correct interpretation of the hadith about God's palm (كف) during the ascension?
A) It means God has a literal hand
B) It is a metaphor for God's administration and gentleness
C) It refers to the Prophet's own hand
D) It is a symbol of punishment

Key Takeaway
The hadith about God's palm is understood metaphorically as a sign of His gentle administration, not a literal limb.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
When you read the hadith about God's palm, did your mind immediately form a mental image of a hand? Why is it so hard to detach from that image, and what does that say about your reliance on your own imagination over scriptural guidance?
?
The Prophet felt 'coolness' as spiritual comfort from God's gentle administration. In your life, when have you experienced a moment of peace that you attributed to God's direct care? How can you train yourself to recognize such moments as acts of divine gentleness rather than random events?
?
This lesson teaches that God's palm is not a limb but a metaphor for His control. Are you willing to submit to His administration even when it feels uncomfortable? What is one area of your life where you are resisting His gentle guidance, and what will you do today to surrender it?

The First Proof: Musa's Request
First proof from Musa's request for vision.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand the first proof from Musa's verse for the possibility of seeing Allah, based on the fact that a prophet would not ask for the impossible.

Core Idea
A prophet does not ask for the impossible.

This lesson examines the first of two arguments from the Qur'anic verse of Musa (7:143) for the possibility of ru'ya. The argument centers on the fact that Musa, a prophet and intimate interlocutor, asked to see Allah. Since a prophet would not ask for something known to be impossible, ru'ya must be possible.

Guided Path
1
Read the passage and translation
Read the Arabic passage and its literal translation carefully. Notice how the argument is structured as a disjunction (either knowledge or ignorance).
2
Identify the two alternatives
The argument presents two possibilities: Musa either knew ru'ya is impossible or he was ignorant. Identify how each alternative leads to a contradiction.
3
Reflect on the role of prophethood
Consider why ignorance would disqualify someone from prophethood. The passage says the purpose of prophethood is to call to true beliefs.
4
Understand the conclusion
Since both alternatives are impossible, the initial assumption that ru'ya is impossible must be false. Thus ru'ya is possible.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
قدمه لأنه الأصل في هذا الباب ) والعمدة) من المنقولات في ذلك ( قوله تعالى حكاية عن موسى عليه السلام و رب أرني أنظر إليك قال لن تراني ولكن أنظر إلى الجبل فإن استقر مكانه فسوف تراني ﴾ [الأعراف : ١٤٣]، والاحتجاج به من وجهين: الأول: أن موسى عليه السلام ( سأل الرؤية ولو امتنع كونه تعالى مرئياً (لما سأل لأنه حينئذ إما أن يعلم امتناعه أو يجهله فإن علمه فالعاقل لا يطلب المحال فإنه عبث، وإن جهله فالجاهل بما لا يجوز على الله ويمتنع لا يكون نبياً كليما، وقد وصفه الله تعالى بذلك في كتابه بل ينبغي أن لا يصلح للنبوة إذا المقصود من البعثة هو الدعوة إلى العقائد الحقة والأعمال الصالحة ( الثاني : أنه ( تعالى ( علق الرؤية على استقرار الجبل واستقرار الجبل أمر ممكن في نفسه وما علق على الممكن فهو ممكن، إذ لو كان ممتنعاً لأمكن صدق الملزوم بدون صدق اللازم ) قوله : ( وإن جهله إلخ ) حاصله أن ثبوت الجهل يستلزم انتفاء النبوة والنبوة ثابتة فينتفي الجهل ويثبت العلم بالامتناع على تقدير تحققه ومعلوم الامتناع لا يسأله العاقل مع أن السؤال متحقق فتعين الإمكان. ، قوله : ( وما علق على الممكن فهو ممكن) أورد عليه أنه يصح أن يقال : إن انعدم المعلول انعدمت العلة، والعلة قد يمتنع عدمه والسر فيه أن الارتباط بين الشرط والجزاء بحسب الوقوع الإمكان وذلك لأن إمكان الشيء ذاتي غير معلق على شيء، وأجيب بأن انعدام العلة التامة على قاعدة الإسلام غير ممتنع إذ منها تعلق القدرة والإرادة ويجوز انقطاعه وفيه أنه يشكل بالنسبة إلى الصفات وقد يجاب بأن المراد بالممكن المعلق عليه هو الذي في مرتبة الإمكان الصرف بحيث لا يشوبه امتناع لا من الذات ولا من الغير ولا شك في أن إمكان استقرار الجبل كذلك ولا كذلك انعدام المعلول فيما امتنع عدم علته وأما ما ذكر من السر فستعرف جوابه وفيه نظر لأن ارادة الله تعالى تعلقت بعدم استقراره عقيب النظر فاستحال استقراره لذلك وإن كانت استمالة بالعرض، ويمكن أن يجاب عن أصل الاعتراض بمنع صحة ذلك القول لغة فتأمل ..
He prioritized it because it is the foundation in this chapter and the main transmitted evidence for that is the saying of the Exalted, narrating from Musa, peace be upon him: 'My Lord, show me [Yourself] that I may look at You. He said: You will not see Me, but look at the mountain; if it remains in its place, then you will see Me.' (Al-A'raf 7:143). And arguing by it is from two aspects: First: that Musa, peace be upon him, asked for vision (al-ru'ya), and if it were impossible for the Exalted to be visible, he would not have asked, because then either he knows its impossibility or he is ignorant of it. If he knows it, then a rational person does not seek the impossible for it is futile. If he is ignorant of it, then one ignorant of what is not permissible for God and is impossible cannot be a prophet and intimate interlocutor (nabiyyan kaliman), when God has described him with that in His book. Rather, he should not be fit for prophethood, since the purpose of sending is the call to true beliefs and righteous deeds. Second: that He, Exalted, conditioned vision upon the settling of the mountain, and the settling of the mountain is a matter possible in itself, and what is conditioned upon the possible is possible, for if it were impossible, it would be possible for the consequent to be true without the antecedent being true. His saying: 'And if he is ignorant etc.' Its summary is that the establishment of ignorance necessitates the negation of prophethood, and prophethood is established, so ignorance is negated and knowledge of impossibility is established on the supposition of its actuality, and the known impossible is not asked by a rational person while the question is actual, so possibility is determined. His saying: 'And what is conditioned upon the possible is possible' – it was objected to him that it is correct to say: If the effect ceases, the cause ceases, and the cause may be impossible to cease. The secret in it is that the connection between the condition and the recompense is according to the occurrence of possibility, because the possibility of a thing is intrinsic, not conditioned upon anything. And it was answered that the cessation of the complete cause according to the rule of Islam is not impossible, since from it are the attachment of power and will, and its interruption is permissible. There is in it that it is problematic with respect to the attributes. And it may be answered that what is meant by the possible which is conditioned upon is that which is in the rank of pure possibility, such that no impossibility mixes with it from itself or from another. There is no doubt that the possibility of the settling of the mountain is like that, and not so the cessation of the effect in what makes the cessation of its cause impossible. As for what was mentioned of the secret, you will know its answer. And there is in it consideration because the will of God was attached to its not settling after the looking, so its settling became impossible for that reason, even if it is impossible by accident. And it can be answered about the original objection by denying the correctness of that statement linguistically. So reflect.
Source pages p. 132

Commentary
This passage presents two proofs from the Qur'anic verse of Musa (alayh al-salam) that it is possible to see Allah (ru'ya). The first proof is from the fact that Musa, a prophet, asked for ru'ya; a prophet would not ask for something impossible, so ru'ya must be possible. The second proof is from the conditional statement: Allah says 'if the mountain remains in its place, then you will see Me.' Since the settling of the mountain is possible in itself, and the consequent (ru'ya) is conditioned on a possible event, the consequent is also possible. The passage then includes glosses on these proofs. The first gloss explains that if Musa were ignorant of the impossibility, he would not be a prophet; since he is a prophet, he must have known it is possible. The second gloss addresses an objection that conditioning on possibility does not guarantee possibility if the cause becomes impossible. The answer distinguishes pure possibility from conditional impossibility, noting that Allah's will to not settle the mountain after the look does not negate the intrinsic possibility of settling. The passage concludes with a linguistic argument against the objection.

Key Terms
الرؤية
المحال
النبوة

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: Some might think that a prophet could ask for the impossible out of ignorance or as a test.
Correction: The argument shows that a prophet must have knowledge of divine attributes; ignorance would disqualify him from prophethood. Therefore, Musa's request indicates he knew ru'ya is possible.

Checkpoint
According to the first proof, why would Musa's request for ru'ya be impossible if ru'ya were impossible?
A) Because a prophet would not ask for something he knows to be impossible.
B) Because Musa was ignorant of the impossibility.
C) Because the mountain would not settle.
D) Because the verse was abrogated.

Key Takeaway
Musa's request for ru'ya proves its possibility because a prophet does not ask for the impossible.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
When you make duʿā’, do you ever hold back from asking something because you think it is too big or impossible? How does Musa’s example teach you to trust in Allah’s power?
?
The proof shows that a prophet must know what is permissible for Allah. Do you truly know the attributes of Allah, or are there areas where you are ignorant? How does that ignorance affect your worship and duʿā’?
?
Musa asked for the ultimate vision of Allah. What is the greatest thing you have ever asked Allah for? If you have never asked for something that requires complete reliance on His absolute power, what stops you?
